<Author>Jill_Downunder
<Content>Fantastic hotel - a real find in Amsterdam I stayed here on two occasions, each for one night, on business. This is a top quality hotel in a great location in Amsterdam (right on one of Amsterdam's lovely canals). The staff were helpful, friendly and polite from the minute I walked in the door and till the minute I left. Not speaking Dutch is no problem as all the staff I spoke to have excellent English skills.The room was tastefully and stylishly decorated. The bed was very comfortable, and the bathroom facilities were well presented and very clean. The room was typical size for European hotels, but I didn't actually feel cramped or cluttered, and the furnishings and decor were really attractive and created a pleasant atmosphere.It is the little things that really make this place stand out. For example, there is a small minibar in the room - and it's completely included. There are spirits, beer, wine - all included in the price. Downstairs in the lounge, near reception, there is also a drinks/nibbles bar, from mid-afternoon onwards, where you can get free drinks and nibbles. No charge for anything - that includes more expensive drinks like Baileys, Tia Maria, etc as well as a range of wines, beers, and other spirits. There is also a nice selection of nibblies (cheese, crackers, nuts, olives).The hotel provides two internet browsing stations in the lounge - and they're free to use, as well. And breakfast is also included in the room rate. Breakfast is great - a very good selection of cereals, fruits, cold meats, and some hot food (bacon, sausages) and they will make you your eggs however you like them (scrambled, fried, omelette etc). It really conveys a much more personal feel than most hotels in most big cities.It's also quite conveniently located - about a 10 minute walk to Anne Frank's house (and the Prinsengracht area in general, which borders on the lovely Jordaan region, with lots of interesting shops, small streets, cafes), very close to the flower market, and the canal bus has a stop not too far away (fantastic option when you're too tired to do any more walking!) Overall, this was a real find. I'd stay here again in a heartbeat. Nothing ever seemed too much trouble for the staff, and the quality and service were excellent.

<Author>Hotelreviewer_C
<Content>My Favourite Hotel I've stayed in quite a few hotels around Europe over the last few years, and at Bank Mansion I had my best ever hotel experience. In a world full of soulless chains and dives, this character laden gem is really one of a kind.We visited the hotel (couple, mid twenties) Nov '08 on a short weekend trip to Amsterdam. The staff were very kind, courteous and as everything in the hotel was complementary, I feel that they treated all customers the same.Free Bar! Seriously. Couldn't believe it. Beer in the fridges, wine on ice, bottles of spirits, mixers, coffee machine and always a selection of nibbles (cheese, nuts, olives, etc). Free drinks in the room as well!!!Other reviewers complained about the size of the room, room service options etc. But they obviously chose the wrong hotel for their needs. I hate being ripped off, so I never order room service or use minibars, or watch pay per view films. Here there were no hidden charges. No charge for Breakfast, minibar, bar, internet etc. It drives me up the wall when you book a posh hotel for a hefty sum and are forced to pay extra to use the internet or watch a film or whatever. So I suppose it's all relative. Some won't like this hotel. But I stand by what I said earlier, you are treated better at Banks Mansion because nobody is paying extra. The staff don't look down at you because you haven't racked up a massive drinks/food bill or aren't booking in for hourly herbal massage treatments. With all the conventions, hidden charges etc, I've found it hard to be truly comfortable in highly rated 5 star hotels that I've visited.Others: Room was nice, stylish. Bathroom gorgeous. No view, but didn't request one (2 day stay in November....)Lobby and Living room area were also very stylish and comfortable. Nice realistic gas fire. Some lovely furniture throughout the hotel too.Breakfast is as good as you will get on the continent. Omelettes/Pancakes/Eggs all made fresh for you (no extra charge)Very nice area. If you, like us want a comfortable base from where to explore the city where you can unwind with a free drink or more and are not overly concerned about over rated 5 star luxuries, then book this hotel.

<Author>grebliv
<Content>Tiny rooms, good location, one bad front desk attendant We arrived at Banks Mansion to find ourselves in a 200-300 square foot room, with a canal view, but that was just about the only nice thing about this hotel. Sure, there are three glass carafes of alcohol in the room, a mini-bar which gets restocked daily by the maids, and a coffee machine in the lobby, but for me, the open glass containers of liquor seemed particularly unsafe - as a previous guest could easily put whatever they want inside them and the next guest would never know (they are merely refilled, not new for each guest). The window/doors overlooking the canal were openable, sort of, as the side of the bed was within 2 feet of that wall, and the room was only 3 feet wider than the length of the bed anyway. It made for a lot of zig zagging around to get past the furniture to look out the window. We wanted to change rooms, but there weren't any better/larger ones, other than the honeymoon suite, which already had occupants. We told the front desk person, Pamela, that we would let her know by the next morning if we were going to move to a new hotel, but as we were only staying for 3 days, we decided to just deal with the cramped quarters and try to have a good time outside the room. The next morning Pamela called and asked whether we were leaving. We confirmed that we were going to stay, as we would have told her otherwise by 10am. When we left the hotel to sight-see around 11am, Pamela accosted us and basically demanded that we check out. She had told another person that they could have our room, even though we never said we were actually leaving. She was extremely rude, and was trying to salvage herself due to her own poor decision to try to book the room without confirmation from us that we were leaving. She argued with my boyfriend for about 30 minutes as we were leaving, and made me feel very uncomfortable in that I wasn't sure if she was crazy enough to actually move our things from the room and kick us out. I hoped it wouldn't come to that, but this was my first trip to Europe, so I wasn't sure! Once my boyfriend got tired of arguing with her he told her to sort it out with American Express, and I guess that must have convinced her to give up on trying to kick us out. I spent the entire day somewhat worried about it though until we got back that evening to find our room still accessible by keycard. I wish we had never even gone into that hotel. The hotel is located just around the corner from Rembrandtplein, which is a reasonably safe area with coffee shops, restaurants, and vendors. I definitely do NOT recommend Banks Mansion! Stay elsewhere and you will be much happier!

<Author>YMLSydney
<Content>Great option for exploring Amsterdam Lovely hotel in great location in Amsterdam. We spent most days out and about and would drop in to the hotel for 'lunch/afternoon' tea from the complimentary all day open bar (drinks and snacks plus internet access) and head back out again all afternoon until pre-dinner drinks at the hotel bar again! So we probably saved a bit of money on lunches and cocktails and it was very nice to have a sense of feeling 'at home' in the hotel without having to put our hands into our pockets for everything. Rooms are a little squeezy but clean and tasteful. If you are going to Amsterdam, hiring a bicycle for the duration is a great idea as you can cover lots of ground and even head on out to their lovely countryside in no time. This is a very nice hotel if you want a very comfortable and convenient stay in Amsterdam.

<Author>Lucy_Jones
<Content>Another tripadvisor triumph! Tripadvisor strikes again! We booked this hotel because of the reviews on this site and we were not disappointed. Its in a great location in a nice part of Amsterdam close to all the major sights. We had a canal view room which was nice, but maybe not worth the extra money - depends on how highly you value these things I suppose. The rooms are also not that big, as other reviewers have said, although I don't think this is uncommon for Amsterdam. It was clean and the staff were always really friendly. The hotel has a free bar downstairs in the lobby where you can help yourself to free drinks - tea, coffee, alcohol, soft drinks - all day. There are also small snacks available depending on the time of day. It was a really nice touch and gave the place some life - sometimes hotel bars can be a bit desolate but this one always had a good atmosphere. There are no extra charges for most things - including minibar and breakfast. The breakfast was really good - lots of choice and nice quality food. Overall we were really happy with our stay and felt we had excellent value for money given everything that was included. We'd stay here again if we were back in Amsterdam.

<Content>Central, cosy and friendly Very central, so easy to nip back and change clothes, when weather changes, oh have a free cuppa or beer - yes all drinks and free and can be consumed in very comfy surroundings, swamped with newspapers. <Author>CWYC
<Content>Perfect for a weekend away We spent 2 nights here on a weekend away and I would thoroughly recommend it.It 鈥榙oes what is says on the tin鈥?- it鈥檚 not a hip or luxury boutique hotel by any stretch of the imagination but it is comfortable and it is very convenient, hence I gave it a 4.The front-desk staff are very friendly and helpful. Check-in was quick and the receptionist took us up to the room. We stayed in a canal view room (room 206) which was basically at the apex of the building above the front entrance overlooking the corner of Herengracht and Vijzelstraat. It was a triangular shaped room and while not huge, it wasn鈥檛 poky. The interiors are pleasant enough although not my style. The furniture is a cherry-wood colour and the wardrobes and bedside cabinets have art deco style floral stained glass panels. Breakfast was a standard buffet type affair with a small menu that is cooked-to-order and it was all very nice.The 鈥楲iving Room鈥?area in the lobby and is a nice touch 鈥?free drinks (including branded alcohol) and snacks at all times of the day. Oh, and the mini-bar in the room is also free. Unusual for a hotel in this price range. We loved the location of this hotel on Herengracht, which is beautiful, and the hotel is about 5 minutes walk to the Golden Curve. It鈥檚 convenient to walk to most of the major museums within 20 minutes. There are 3 tram lines from outside the hotel which are also very handy. Oh, and there鈥檚 a Canalbus stop on Herengracht about 5 minutes walk from the hotel.The only downside we experienced was that the housekeeping staff knocked on our door at 9.45am on Sunday morning to ask when they would be able to clean our room. Given that we were checking out that day, and check-out is at 12pm, we thought that was a bit unnecessary. On the whole though, we enjoyed our stay - it was fuss, and hassle free and we will stay there again next time we go back to Amsterdam.

<Author>Moley8
<Content>Somewhere special My partner and I booked a last minute stay at the Banks Mansion and from the moment the reservation was made, the staff proved how important it is to make the customer feel special. We had a problem with the credit card when booking and the following day the hotel made contact, by telephone as well as email, and ensured that the reservation was made without worrying about taking a deposit. We arrived pretty early on our first day and intended to drop our bags and run, but the lovely Nena told us the room was nearly ready and showed us down to the breakfast room and offered us complimentary breakfast while we waited. How often does that happen....??! The room was a large room on the ground floor, facing the road, when we enquired about moving Nena was only too happy to look at the other rooms and quickly moved us up to the 2nd floor, overlooking the canal. The room was small and the art deco style might not be to everyones taste but it was very clean, comfortable and with the lovely bathroom and huge shower with rainfall head it was perfect. A well stocked, complimentary(!!), minibar with additional decanters of spirits, robes and flipflop slippers were the icing on the cake.The 'living room' area in reception offers complimentary wines, beers, spirirts and hot drinks along with snacks and newspapers so you can chill out after a long day exploring this fantastic city.The staff were excellent throughout our 2 night stay and nothing was too much trouble for them. As we had an early morning flight home, Nena organised cereals, milk and fruit to be left in our room the night before. Again, nothing proved to be too much trouble and the staff were genuinely happy to help. We will definitely stay here again when we next visit Amsterdam, which might not be too far away.....

<Author>dpglasgow
<Content>One of the few hotels worth repeated visits in Amsterdam I've stayed in this hotel on three occasions and it has never disappointed. It's comfortable, classy without being pretentious, and each time the staff have been very helpful. But the best thing of all is that drinks and snacks are absolutely free. At first we couldn't quite grasp the idea that a hotel would give you free drinks in your room (yes, including alcoholic ones) and a wide range of free drinks in the 'Living' area downstairs, including wines, beers, soft drinks and coffee, supplemented by a range of nibbles that changes over the course of the day. I've noticed that other Carlton hotels don't do this - it seems that only in Amsterdam do they trust guests not to abuse the privilege. It makes for a very relaxing experience. The hotel really is everything it says on its website.

<Author>downhudson
<Content>Welcome respite in busy Amsterdam We were given a recommendation to the Banks Mansion by our hotel clerk in the Hague. The big plus was that every service within the hotel is free. There was a lovely breakfast, in the dedicated room downstairs, with station for omelets, pancakes, etc., delicious breads, cold meats, salmon. In the late afternoon, the cocktail hour offerings included wine, beer, soda and little snacks (nuts, olives, chips). There were also copies of manyinternational newspapers, which along with the food, insured that there was a friendly busy quality to the confortably appointed hotel lobby in the late afternoon. The internet was also free access, including two computer stations. The entire hotel, which is small, a boutique hotel, four floors,is decorated in the style of Frank Lloyd Wright's decorative stained glass, and geometric patterns. Many design details have been thoughtfully incorporated (an under sink night light in the bathroom, for example; lighted cabinets). The room rate was slightly higher than our normal budget (229 Euros per/night), but we found the extra offerings plus the desk hospitality and advice about the city well worth the higher rate. We were given a corner room which overlooked the street, with an oblique view toward the famous Herengracht canal. Great peaceful location! Given the many warnings about the difficulties of finding a good hotel in Amsterdam, this one was a quiet and comforting place to land at the end of much walking and museum visits in Amsterdam.

<Author>flyboy411
<Content>Be Careful! This place is really different - and a mixed bag. No stupid rip-offs with the mini-bar, lots of terrific extras - all 'free' and a really great location. BUT, the breakfast was about as poor a standard as could be imagined, eg scrambled eggs made by reheating already-made stuff resembling yellow rubber, poor selection etc. This is not what hotel dining rooms should offer. The safe was broken, the phone didn't work, and they would only move us to a different room at OUR expense. The free WiFii turned out to last 50 minutes and in one room didn't work at all. Hmmm.The worst part was that our foursome booked for 2 days and were forced to leave after one due to genuine and serious circumstances beyond our control. We asked (at breakfast time) if they would let us off the second night's charge. The (young) guy at the desk was very tough and said he would 'ask his manager', later saying he did so and was told 'no'. I said I expected a more lenient attitude under the circumstances and wanted to speak to the manager myself and he immediately said 'OK, we will let you off one room but not both. We can't lose money because of your problems.' I later discovered that they managed to fill the entire hotel that night but still pocketed the room charge they demanded from us.I know we had booked for 2 nights and technically, they may be said to be in the right, but I doubt the manager was even consulted and whereas the small things are what could make this hotel so attractive, knowing they employ transparently poor actors like him and are happy to 'fine' us a (not inexpensive) room rate they ANYWAY sold to somebody else, makes me reluctant to set foot there again or recommend them. You need to feel comfortable in a hotel, but they run it so poorly it spoiled the whole experience.

<Author>My_Aunt
<Content>Lived up to its promise My husband and I stayed at the Banks Hotel for seven nights (April 30 - May 8), and we were very satisfied with the hotel. I booked directly with the hotel, and I was contacted by the desk staff to welcome us and enquire about any requests. And we did have a couple of requests: 1) we were arriving in the morning and asked to check earlier than the usual time 2) we asked for a room that had a bath tub (most rooms have showers). The staff replied promptly, saying that they will try to accommodate our requests - and they did. We were checked in by Nina, who is very efficient, knowledgeable, and friendly, and so are the rest of the desk staff - Pamela, Laura, Kevin and Ali. Our corner room commanded a view of the canal (Herengracht) and the street (Vijzelstraat). The room and the bathroom were spacious and comfortable. We travel in Europe once a year, so we are used to smaller (than North American) rooms. Breakfast in the kitchen was also very good; omelettes, pancakes and French toast can be ordered in addition to the buffet-style standards (cheese, cold cuts, smoked salmon, etc.); however, the selection wasn't changed when we were there. The 24-hour lounge snacks and drinks were also good, keeping in mind that these are snacks and not mini-meals, along the lines of nuts, olives, Dutch waffles (cookies), and the occasional dips and cheese.I would have rated the hotel excellent, but the housekeeping service leaves much to be desired. In our 7-day stay, we had to ask 4 times for bathroom items that were lacking: soap, shower gels, bath salts. In addition, the cleaning was cursory: empty gel bottles and soiled face cloths were left uncollected. But again, the desk staff was very quick in sending whatever we needed. As a matter of fact, one of them came to our room with the items that were missing, and she saw the condition of the bathroom.The location was also ideal for us. It was central enough, but not too busy like the Dam, Rembrandtplein or Leidseplein. We like walking, so we walked to many of the the attractions, occasionally taking the tram to the Central Station or the Museum area.Aside from the problem with housekeeping, we were happy with the level of service, specifically of the desk staff ,and would recommend Banks Mansion Hotel.

<Author>jc2k
<Content>Best In Town Banks Mansion was the first hotel my wife and I stayed at when we started to go to Amsterdam for a city break about three years ago. We thought that it was lovely then; the free snacks, drinks and tv were all excellent, as was the location and all this made our stay wonderful.We have been back to Amsterdam several times since but stayed in different hotels and this last time, we returned to Banks Mansion again. Having now had the experience of staying in other amsterdam hotels, I can honestly say that the best is definitely Banks. The quality of the decor, size of the room, location and the hospitality cannot be faulted. The breakfast was great, meaning we only had to have a snack for lunch and the air con was effective and not too noisy in the room.Only slight minor side is that the lift is very slow and if you are on the top floor, it's often quicker to walk! Other than that, lovely hotel, sure its a bit pricey but I certainly didn't feel ripped off with what we paid. Definitely recommended.

<Content>Wonderful Hotel Stayed at the Bank's Mansion for four nights in April and couldn't have been more pleased. Location was great and in walking distance to a lot of attractions. Small restaurant across the street, Peking, had very good sandwiches, soup, Dutch pancakes and after 4 pm they have Chinese food. <Author>walkerSuffolk
<Content>Excellent hotel A great hotel situated in central Amsterdam, within easy walking distance of most sights in the city. The hotel is immaculate and the staff most helpful and pleasant. The unusual feature of the Banks is that you are provided with decanters of whisky, brandy and gin in the room with mixers and soft drinks, all included in the price. The room was large and comfortable. In the lobby there is a comfortable seating area with sofas and armchairs, coffee, tea etc and a bar with wines,spirits, even champagne, and snacks available all day,again all included in the price. The breakfast was excellent and could fill you up for the day if you wanted. They don't serve dinner but there are so many restaurants in Amsterdam that you wouldn't really want to eat at the hotel. You can find cheaper hotels but for my wife and I we would stay at the Banks Mansion again when we return to Amsterdam.

<Author>bobolito
<Content>Great experience This was our first stay at this hotel and we loved it and will return.Highlights were: the corner room...this is a must. There is more room and more light in these units facing the front of the hotel. Ask ahead of time. Even with the windows opened, you couldn't really step out on to balcony because there was not much room. There are better views around town but other things in this hotel make up for the lack of a balcony. Rooms are small but extremely functional and charming.The complementary beverage and food in lobby was great. We invited a friend over after a long day and enjoyed just sitting in front of the fire place drinking and snacking and enjoying it all. We liked getting extra water and coffee from this area to bring to room. NIce chocolates and rotating snacks all day long if you happened to be there. Bar in room and frig for other things.Free WI Fi in lobby at two big desks. You could check in on any info without using your room computer. They also gave you 50 minutes free WI FI in room.Bathrooms were great...not huge but perfectly set. Great big tub and fantastic rain shower. Very clean. Ice and shoe shine right at the end of the hallway.Bed was nice and hard but I did not like the seam down the middle. This would be so easy to correct with a proper pad over the seam! Pillows were rather lumpy.Breakfast down stairs in the basement was fabulous. We missed the first morning because we slept in but the second day we enjoyed all the goodies. Great selection of papers and magazines at breakfast and in lobby each day.The front desk was outstanding! Great help and extremely friendly.The only thing I thought odd was the lack of vacuuming of the carpet in all of the hall ways. This made its seem dirty but I could just tell that it really had not been vacuumed well...or in a long time. Odd... when every thing else was very clean.GREAT LOCATION.The tram was just outside hotel a block up. Very easy to get to train station, 10 minute ride. Not on a super busy street but close to every thing. Flower mart was 2 blocks away. Great cafes near by.Fabulous hotel... we will be back.

<Author>peace3030
<Content>Cozy comfort and class This was my fifth trip to Amsterdam and I've stayed at a variety of hotels around town. The Banks Mansion is the best by far - the location, the comfort and service were absolutely top-notch. The 'living-room' will make the traveler feel like they are back at home - but better. Fabulous and fresh breakfast, in-room movies and a well stocked mini-bar are just a few of the perks. This is more for the business or older couple traveler - you could not be more central to trams and shopping districts as well as museums. Ask for a canal view room! Not recommended for anyone coming to experience the 'alternative' parts of Amsterdam.

<Author>Amijoe
<Content>Lovely relaxing atmosphere, great location We stayed at the Banks Mansion for a long anniversary weekend last summer, and it was perfect. The hotel's living room for guests is a fantastic concept, a great place to come back to and relax with whatever you'd like to drink and little snacks, comfy chairs and magazines to read - I'd pop down from our room with a book and curl up by the fire if hubby wanted a pre-dinner nap. I really enjoyed the living room and made the most of it, spending the early evenings chatting with other guests as we all came down for an early evening drink before parting ways for the night.The staff were friendly and helped with directions or recommendations for evening walks or canal trips. The hotel itself is in a fantastic location on one of Amsterdam's most beautiful canals, and is also a brief walk to Rembrandt Square where there's plenty of late night cafe and bar culture for an evening out - we'd sit and people watch every evening for hours. The hotel's also conveniently located for frequent trams, so you can take a leisurely stroll through the tulip market and along canals/shops up to the train station then hop on a tram back if the weather turns (the hotel has umbrellas for guests if it does turn wet).The rooms aren't big by anyone's standards but they're beautifully put together in a modern deco/Charles Rennie Mackintosh style, and our bathroom was beautifully finished with an enormous rainfall shower. The little touches are nice - our room had a few cut glass decanters with different (and tasty!) spirits for a night cap. The room and hotel both were nicer than 5* resorts/hotels I've stayed in, the bed linen good quality and the mattress comfortable. The room was spotless, as was the entire hotel. I'd completely recommend this hotel to anyone wanting a comfortable break in a convenient location, and would return in a heartbeat.  
<Date>Feb 14, 2008

<Author>roundtheworld321
<Content>A Quality Establishment This is a quality establishment. The staff are extremely professional and all seem to speak impecable English, service is of a very high standard. There is no bar as such but the very pleasant lounge area has a self service bar with a choice of different bottled beers, wines, spirits and soft drinks all included at no extra charge within the room rate. The all inclusive drinks extends to the mini bar in the room. Our mini bar was very well stoked with beer, soft drinks and chocolate bars and there were also 3 decanters of spirits. The room was not particularly spacious but was well presented. The bathroom was of a good standard and the bed was very comfortable. We had to pay extra for a canal view but it was worth it. The hotel has a breakfast room but no dining room which necesitates going out for dinner but as the hotel is very centrally located there are plenty of very good places to eat within a short walking distance. This is a nice place to stay if you are visiting Amsterdam

<Content>Fantastic, Fantastic,Fantastic I booked this hotel , direct, as part of a 3 night / 4day trip to Amsterdam.I was told about this by a good friend of mine.The hotel is just around the corner from Rembrant Square, and 200 mtrs from the no.4 tram stop.the outside of the hotel is nothing special, but when you climb the steps (only 4 or 5) and enter the lounge/reception area, you get a feeling of something special.The staff are friendly, professional and very helpful. one lady Nina, is a credit to the hotel !!!The 'Lounge' area is relaxed with comfy chairs and sofas, a fire in one corner, and NO Television !!!There is a bar that comes as complementary as part of your rate.The rooms are a decent size not massive, just right. <Author>FlossChester
<Content>Lovely experience We have just returned from a weekend break in Amsterdam - we had gone over especially to see 'Night at the Proms' in Rotterdam. As usual, I checked out Trip Advisor and selected this hotel based on other peoples' recommendations.The directions to the hotel are clearly shown on its website - number 16 or 24 tram from Central Station, 4th stop. It is then just a 50m walk to the hotel from the stop.The location was great. Despite being by a fairly busy road the rooms was very quiet (I am a light sleeper) - and also very warm considering the cold outside!There is a great atmosphere in the lobby area as residents meet up for their complimentary snacks, hot drinks or something stronger! There is a living flame fire which is especially cosy for this time of the year.We paid for a delux room and had a fab view over the Kaisersgracht canal (not sure that's spelt correctly). The decor was beautiful and I loved the big shower.The staff were very helpful. The breakfast was great - I loved the pancakes whereas my husband went straight for the 'full English' option. The only thing I could fault was there being no bath - which I was aware of before I booked, but, with all the walking around a good soak would've been beneficial!

<Author>cashew_nut
<Content>Just okay. Not more than 3 stars. My boyfriend and I have just returned from a two night stay at the Banks Mansion. We booked because of the great reviews on TA but had such a bad experience I felt I needed to write my own review.Although it is undeniably in a great location - no more than 10mins walk to everywhere it seemed, and just around the corner from the picturesque '9 streets' - the hotel is just not worth the money.Our room (212) was incredibly dark - we felt like we were in the basement despite being on the 2nd floor, and was really way too small to justify the 279Euros it costs a night. We could hardly walk around the bed - and had no-where to put our luggage. On the plus side the bed was very comfy however the pillows were lumpy and really need to be replaced. FYI - Banks Mansion claims to have a 'pillow menu' - but they didn't have any pillows available when we asked so the claim seemed a bit of a let down! We also only had one pair of slippers and one dressing gown. The drinks in the 'free minibar' were never replenished, and after the room was cleaned on Saturday morning the maid left old half full cans of coke and beer.Finally, the room was not clean (by my standards) - hair in the bath and in the sink, soap marks on the mirror, grit on the carpet in the bedroom, and dark marks all over the wallpaper. FYI - our room was non-smoking but everything including the bathroom towels smelt smoky and dusty. The communal areas - lounge etc are also smoking so it cannot be avoided in this hotel. The free nibbles (always the same..nuts and crisps, nougat and small waffles) and drinks were great but again they did not make up for the room. The very last bone of contention about this hotel is the breakfast. It's really quite horrible. The pancakes (made to order) come out of a packet and are literally warmed up on the griddle in front of you. The eggs are worse - they have a tub of orange eggy liquid which they pour into a frying pan...) There were no pastries or croissants, etc. Not much choice at all to be honest. All in all, based on our experience we would not recommend this hotel. There were simply too many problems to justify the price, and even if we had loved our room it is still too expensive.Hope you find this review useful.

<Author>Chem73
<Content>Amazing hotel in a great city Believe all of the reviews here, this is a brilliant hotel. We booked from reading the reviews here. It can look a bit more expensive than a lot of the hotels in Amsterdam but the accomodation and use of facilities is worth every penny. The free bar was well stocked with loads of chocolate, biscuits, etc. The beer and wine was all good quality and at various times during the day extra food was put out. It was a great area to go to unwind after a busy day in amsterdam.Breakfast was also included in the rate (we found the best deal via opodo.co.uk) which was a very good range of food and anything you needed made up to order.In the room the free mini-bar was well stocked with chocolate and drinks, the in house movies were also included in the price. I don't think any hotel rooms in Amsterdam are particularly large but the rooms were modern, clean and very comfortable.The location is also very good, right by the flower market and a short walk to almost all attractions. Probably a 15 minute walk from the central station or accessable on the tram routes.If your off to Amsterdam you have to try this hotel - it is as good as every review here.

<Author>BenL1
<Content>Great stay at Banks Mansion I recently spent four days at Banks Mansion during a long weekend. We both loved it and would recommend it to friends. The location is great as it is equidistant between the centre of town and the museum area- we walked pretty much everywhere all weekend but the tram was outside the door if you wanted it. Also it is on one of the main canals, but it is far enough away from the neon lights and really touristy squares to feel really relaxed (although there is a sqaure with all this only a block away if you want it). Room was nicely done with massive walk-in shower and art deco styling. We didnt have a canal view as all were booked but it was fine and heavy curtains and double glazing kept out all noise from the street. Really nice touch is free mini bar in room and free serve yourself area downstairs- soft drinks, wine, beers, coffee, tea, cava and even spirits. Also free internet. Dont get me wrong, you dont go to Amsterdam to drink all day in the room, but it was really nice to go back to freshen up and have a beer before heading out, or a night cap when returning home. We normally dont use hotel facilities as it always feels a rip-off, but it made it feel really relaxing to be able to do this.

<Author>Sarah_Bedford
<Content>Fabulous trip We stayed here for 3 days in August with some of our family. The way the hotel operates is innovative. A small boutique style place with only 50 rooms and an attentive staff. The hotel is just off the Leidseplein so impossible to get lost as there are signs to it from all areas, and brilliant for walking about.The Living is an area in the foyer stocked with a coffee machine, cold drinks, beer, wine and spirits and allows you to read international papers, use the internet for free, and relax without any need for stress. The service is unobtrusive and there are small snacks available. There is also a minibar and a selection of drinks in the room which makes for a much cheaper stay.Breakfast in bed only costs 5Euros and is wonderful!Some of the rooms have steam rooms within the showers - I'd advise asking for one when you book. None of the rooms have a bath.The Selecta directly opposite the hotel does a great Indonesian ristafel banquet, and there are great Argentinian Steak Houses off the Rembrantsplein.We will definitely stay again - I've stayed in the Pulitzer and Bildeberg Garden hotels and this is far superior.

<Author>Chinsworth
<Content>A Wonderful Time We've been to Amsterdam a dozen times and stayed at medium to very high end places, but this was the most pleasant by far. Having just arrived from a Paris hotel, with all its many gouging charges, we were stunned at the bowls of fruit, snacks, coffee, wine, etc., and the fast internet readily available. There was even a small table with cut glass decanters of brandy and whisky in our room for a private nightcap. Our room was angled at the corner, and we liked the immediacy of the canal and street view, and the modern/retro decorating. Breakfast included eggs and pancakes made to order. We will definitely do this again.

<Author>Nelly-6
<Content>Wonderful! I loved this hotel - a great base for a really relaxing short break in Amsterdam. The whole vibe was very laid back and calm, staff were attentive, with tip-top restaurant recs, and the serve-yourself approach in the lounge was so much nicer than having waiters buzzing around.The room was much bigger and more comfortable than other Amsterdam hotels I've stayed in, although not huge by international standards, but and lets face it, hotels are expensive in this city. The bathroom was large and well-appointed, with an enourmous bath (I could float in it!) and a great walk in shower - but oddly, only one bar of soap was supplied and the bath salts weren't replaced the second day.Breakfast was delicious. There was service at the cooked bar, where eggs, omelettes and pancakes were prepared, and everything else was serve-yourself -so equally as relaxed as the lounge.Overall, I thought the 'all inclusive' concept was worth it for the relaxing vibe - you know if advance what you're paying and don't have to keep a tab on where the minibar bill is heading. And considering the price of Amsterdam hotels, I don't think the room rate is over the top.

<Author>Emily_14
<Content>Extremely Overpriced! Not Worth the Money! I booked this hotel after reading the positive reviews on TripAdvisor. Apparently, most people don't mind paying through the nose for a less-than-mediocre hotel. I stayed for 3 nights in May. I booked a double deluxe room with canal view for over $350/night and I thought I'd be getting my money's worth. What a disappointment! This hotel is nothing more than a Holiday-Inn type chain. The room was really tiny and had cheap stucco-type walls and ceilings. The hotel says it's different because it includes drinks and snacks--this is their gimmick to justify charging such high rates. Your mini-bar is stocked with cans of soda, a couple of waters and some mini bottles of really bad wine. In the lobby you can get more soda and coffee, and... mini Mars bars and other assorted candies. In the afternoons they put out small amounts of bread and butter w/ a very limited amount of cold cuts, which are not replenished when finished. My point is: if their free drinks and snacks feature is supposed to justify their high rates---it's absurd.About the view: I had to stand on my toes to peer out the window and see the canal. Service was standard, and the staff is trained to repeatedly ask you how you are and how your day went EVERYTIME you exit and enter the building.They also ask for a tip when your bill is printed out--there's a blank tip amount line when you sign your bill upon check-out.Overall--no charm, cheaply decorated, tiny rooms, intrusive service--NOT WORTH over $300/night. You'd do better to book a bed  breakfast on the canal and get your money's worth.

<Author>HollowayLondon
<Content>The best part of my holiday was staying at the Banks Mansion Staying at the Banks Mansion was fabulous. When we arrived we were taken to our room, 406, by Pamela, who was so nice throughout our stay. When she opened the door we were overwhelmed by how beautiful the room was. The main room was huge with a large sofa and two armchairs with footstools. There was a widescreen tv and dvd player. The bathroom was divine with a jacuzzi bath and walk-in shower and two sinks. The bedroom, yes seperate bedroom had the biggest bed I have ever seen. When we lay on the bed together and stretched out we did not touch each other. There were 4 windows which overlooked everywhere. The room was so nice we did not even want to go out.It is true the drinks are all complimentary. There is only a small sample of drinks in your room, but downstairs there is a larger variety. Just go and help yourself. There is also snacks and sweets to pig out on all day.Unfortunately, breakfast was not so great. It was just okay. There was not a lot of variety and it was not very tasty. Maybe I am just being fussy.This hotel was in the middle of everything. We did not really need the tram or train tickets because we walked almost everywhere, even late at night. Even though most of the days were sunny, it was always cold, particularly in the shade, and freezing at night. Forget sandals and shorts. Bring comfortable shoes. Forget the party clothes, most people dress casual and comfortable and warm.When you get to the airport, do take the connexions bus return fare for 19.50 euros.The bus will stop about 50m away from the front door. The hotel staff will confirm your return for you, this time the bus will stop right outside. You do not need to buy any maps because everywhere you go someone will give you a map.The best piece of advice I took prior to arriving in Amsterdam was to buy my tickets for Van Gogh museum online, the queue was enormous and we felt quite smug when we just walked straight to the front.If you are going to Amsterdam you will not regret staying at the Banks Mansion.

<Author>Connecticut06
<Content>Wonderful Hotel We recently returned from a 3 night stay at Banks Mansion. I couldn'tfault a thing.We arrived a bit early, and our room wasn't quite ready. The staff atthe front desk were friendly, helpful and capable. We were invited tosit in the lobby and enjoy a snack and drink while waiting. Within 10minutes we were invited upstairs.Our third floor room overlooked the canal. The room was immaculate, and the amenities were wonderful (bathrobes, slippers, room safe, fresh fruit, free mini-bar, decanters of gin  whiskey  congnac). The bed was great, and the hotel is remarkably quiet. The bathroom was fine (shower but no bathtub). All in all, an exceptionally comfortable room.The breakfast room is on the lower level of the hotel. The breakfastbuffet was comprehensive, and could be supplemented by made-to-order eggs, pancakes, omelets, or French toast. I had a wonderful omelet one morning. Again, the service was great.Free drinks of all sorts were always available in the lobby. This included wines, beers, sodas, and even liquers. The hotel is very well located to allow walking to all the major sites in Amsterdam. We never felt the need to take a tram. It was wonderful to be able to stop in the midst of sightseeing for a cold drink and a snack. The staff at the desk provided a very good street map, and were unfailingly polite when we needed replacements, having twice lost ours.The lobby has 2 internet workstations, which I had no trouble accessing whenver I needed. It's a great help to check in and print boarding passes before going to the airport. The hotel will arrange a shuttle to the airport for 24 euros, which worked out well for us--we turned out to be the only 2 passengers, so it was like having our own taxi but cheaper.Do yourself a favor and have an Indonesian dinner at Tempo Doeloe, Utrechtestraat 75. Try a rice platter which includes portions of 18 different dishes. It was among the best meals I have ever had. We've been back in CT for a week and I wish I was in Amsterdam!  
<Date>May 6, 2007

<Author>Rhynette
<Content>Awesome Hotel! I stayed for two nights at the Banks Mansion in late April 2007. I made my reservation directly with the hotel; first good sign - the staff promptly (within a few hours) responded to my e-mail reservation inquiry. From the moment I walked in the door, until the moment I checked out, it was a terrific experience. The staff, ESPECIALLY the front desk staff, were super friendly, helpful, and patient with all my tourist questions. The included breakfast buffet provided tasty, ample selections (sandwich meats, cheeses, omelets, cereals, breads, etc.) from which to energize ones' self at least through lunchtime. My canal-view room was clean, modern, and quiet. The bed was a deliciously comfortable respite from a long day of sightseeing, stocked with 4 plush pillows; goes without saying that I slept VERY WELL!!! Bonuses ranged from an in-room refrigerator stocked with various beverages (included), to individually regulated and responsive air conditioning in the room, to free internet access and daytime snacks/drinks in the lobby. The hotel is centrally located to tourist attractions (many can be reached within 20 minutes' walking time), and a tram line runs right past the hotel which takes you to points north and south in the city. If and when I ever go back to Amsterdam, I already know where I will stay. Great place. Now I know why Banks Mansion is so highly rated by other travelers. I couldn't agree more. Thank you, Banks Mansion, for contributing to my overall delightful and successful visit to Amsterdam!

<Author>gazborangers
<Content>Very disappointing - overpriced! Went to the Banks Mansion for two nights in April. Went with my brother so we booked two rooms. Hotel looks great from the outside but extremely disappointing inside. It looks as though it has been designed with the cheapest of everything possible. It is certainly not a boutique hotel and infact nothing more than a rather poor bed and breakfast. My room was at the back of the hotel. Woodchip celings and two very small windows that I hd to stand on my tip toes to see out. The furniture in the rooms is of chipboard quality and the complimentary mini bar - well laughable. They advertise that all your drinks are free, yes they are if you want to drink cheap Cava, cheap white wine and cheap red wine. You cannot get spirits in the downstairs bar! The staff are very abrupt and the breakfast room is in the basement of the hotel and is reminiscent of a school lunch room. There is no restaurant facilities in the hotel at other times. I would not recommend it to couples for a romantic weekend - it isn't romantic. I think they have some clever marketing but surely they cannot continue to kid everyone all the time.It may be good value if you can drink 48 bottles of beer a day - I sadly couldn't!

<Author>USExPatinUK
<Content>Loved Banks Mansion! My husband and I just returned from 3 days in Amsterdam, staying at the Banks Mansion. What a lovely hotel in a very convenient Amsterdam location! The Banks Mansion is a high quality, smaller hotel (48 rooms) that offers exceptional service and accomodations and is in a great, central location. We paid extra for a 'canal view' room and were not disappointed. The room was very nicely appointed with flat screen TV, large comfortable bed (two twins together), fully stocked bar and beverages (complimentary in our room - not sure if this is available in all rooms). The hotel offers only breakfast service, which is an excellent hot/cold buffet with made to order eggs/omelettes, pancakes, and french toast. The hotel lobby stocks beverages and snacks available to all hotel guests 24 hours a day. The hotel staff is very helpful, suggesting and making restaurant reservations, airport shuttle, etc. The hotel is located within one block of Rembrandt Plein, Munt Plein, and Singel Flower Market. The Museum District and Waterloo Plein are 10 to 15 minutes walk. The hotel is approximately a 25 minute walk from Central Station (depending upon 'crowd' level). I would definately recommend this hotel -- we certainly plan on staying there again on our next trip to Amsterdam.

<Author>ILikeBond
<Content>A Very Pleasant Experience My fiance and I were recently in Amsterdam for 5 days celebrating our engagement. This was a surprise trip for her, so I picked Banks Mansion for our acommodation. We were both very happy with the choice. I asked them to provide flowers for my fiance in the room, which they did, a very beautiful boquet at that. They also put us in a great room, with a beautiful, expansive view of Heren canal.The rain shower was nice, the bath was OK, a little small (fine for 1 person). The luxury touches, like free drinks and snacks, and a pillow menu, were nice, although we only took minimal advantage of them. To me those things weren't really a big deal, but at least they weren't distracting. We only had breakfast there one day, but it was fine, no complaints.I was also impressed with the management's response to an issue that came up. I had booked well in advance, but noticed their prices had dropped, and they were running a special, for the time we would be there. After emailing, they told me to modify my reservation online and I would get the better price. I did that, but I either messed up the process, or somehow the modification wasn't transmitted to them (although I did email them immediately after I had modified it, telling them the same). While I was unable to get the better price before checking out (they told me since they didn't get the info, there was nothing they could do), once I got back state-side, I emailed management about the issue and promptly recieved a return phone call. After explaining the situation, they offered me a credit on a future room or a refund for the amount in the difference in pricing. I chose the later and, indeed, the money was refunded on my credit card. So I appreciated their understanding and acomodation.Finally, the location is great - its right on the edge between what we felt like was the touristy part of Amsterdam (i.e. in between Central Staation and the first of the 3 big canals, Heren Canal), and the more real, residential part of Amsterdam, like the Jordaan area. We enjoyed having access to both, and spent a lot of time walking around some new areas neither of us had yet explored (we've both been to Amsterdam several times). Because its right on Herengraght, too, it makes it easy to walk anywhere East or West. Definitely great location.We would definitely stay here again (and will next time we're in Amsterdam).  
<Date>Mar 13, 2007

<Author>debbieuc
<Content>Excellent hotel, deserves the 5 star reviews Have just returned from a 2 night stay at the Banks Mansion and we were not disappointed. Our room was fairly small (if staying in a canal view room avoid 101/201 etc) but beautifully furnished as were all the other areas of the hotel (with the exception of the garish carpets outside the rooms mentioned in other reviews! ) The free drink and snacks is a wonderful idea and there was plenty available - and good stuff too. Lovely to come back to after a day sightseeing or to sit in the lounge for a cognac before going out. The staff couldn't have been more obliging or friendly and the breakfast was delicious. The hotel is really well placed for sightseeing - accessible by trams 16, 24 or 25 from central but also within walking distance if you miss the last one at midnight.One slight negative is the shower which doesn't seal very well and leads to a very wet floor if you are not careful - but that's a minor moan from an otherwise perfect stay.We thoroughly recommend this hotel and would stay here if ever visiting Amsterdam in the future.

<Author>CATracey
<Content>Fantastic hotel but wished I had a different room This hotel is amazing. Everything about it was wonderful and pretty much how I imagined it would be. We stayed for 3 nights in Feb. I could go on and on about how fabulous the room was and how helpful the staff were and how great all the extras were as other reviewers have done, but I can't really add to what's already been said. Stay here, you will not regret it. It will become your favorite hotel.That being said, I had two very minor disappointments. One being the room given to us (room 101). We had booked a deluxe canal view room months in advance. Upon arrival we were given probably the smallest room in the hotel. The bathroom didn't have a bath, only a shower (a fantastic shower it should be said). But even with a small room minus a bath, it was still fine, we still had a great time. I could've asked to be moved but decided it really wasn't worth the bother. The next time I go, I will ask to see different rooms/configurations and will probably not choose a canal view room (we were hardly there). The second disappointment was the fee charged for wireless connection in the room (10 euros for 60 minutes). Since everything about this hotel is all-inclusive, I didn't understand why wireless wasn't included. There were 2 computers with free internet in the lobby, but for someone like me, working on the go from my laptop, lobby computers were not an option. Banks should either offer free wireless, or find a different internet access provider to offer better rates for their guests.The time we spent in the lobby by the fireplace after a full day of sightseeing was something we will always remember. Thank you Banks, we will be back.

<Author>howarthshome
<Content>Fantastic hotel if you can afford the rate We booked directly over the internet a room with canal view which cost extra and is definitely not a budget price hotel, however, if it fits your budget We can thoroughly recommend it. our room was No 106 on the 1st floor and was decorated stunningly with 3 opening double tall windows looking out onto the canal and main street. Lovely decor, very comfy bed (2 very wide singles pushed together) air con, tv with 2 free porn channels 69 +70 (spice up your weekend - the dutch are definitely not prudes) a superb double size Rain shower and a bath, haidryer etc, plus FREE whisky, conyac and vodka in cut glass decanters and a mini bar stocked with smoothies, coca Cola, beer and fruit juices. That was just the beginning, the staff are so helpful and will recommend eating out etc based upon their experiences. Once you get your bearings you will soon find that you are located in an excellent location whether walking(as we did) or getting buses, taxis or trams. Some of the best places we went were The Ice bar (expensive but worth it) Ranchos Argentinian steak house, Red light district - you will be amazed (just window shopping) Anyway back to the hotel, the breakfasts were great, choice of cooked scambled eggs, bacon and sausage plus fruit, cooked meats, various breads for toast, or your own personally cooked omelette. And in the Living a lovely fire to chill out to when you returned to your hotel each evening with a FREE bar where you just help yourself to beer, wine, spirits and snacks (if there is a bottle that is empty just ask the staff and they will replace it with a full bottle) Then there is the free internet also in the living, by the time you add all the free booze and internet time you soon realise that although it seems a bit expensive when you first book when you check out and your bill is just the same as when you first booked that this hotel is a real find and is actually a bargain.I would recommend this hotel to anyone I know and will definitely stay here next time we visit Amsterdam.I hope the other rooms in the hotel live up to room 106.Personally we will ask for 106 when we go again.Enjoy!!!!

<Author>bellaoes
<Content>Absolutely First Rate Hotel We booked via the hotel website based on trip advisor reviews and stayed 3 nights. We cannot recommend the hotel highly enough. Staff bend over backwards to make sure you have everything you desire (we were offered a choice of 3 seperate rooms with different views/layouts). We also arrived about 4 hours prior to check in time and were provided with a room immediately by the super friendly reception staff. The rooms had terrific canal views and noise was blocked out by double glazing. Rooms had a lovely art deco them and were a great size! The free movies and mini bar/snacks were an excellent touch and I highly recommend the breakfasts - dutch pancakes and the likes made to order. All the attractions are within an easy walking distance ie Heineken museum, Rijksmuseum, Van Gogh, Dam Square, Red Light District etc. (although if going to central you might prefer to take a tram - which leave from the front door). The incredibly friendly staff made the stay even more pleasant. If you are going to Amsterdam you absolutely MUST stay here.

<Author>Hendybug
<Content>Fantastic City Centre Hotel Banks Mansion is not your usual European City Centre hotel. It is much more in keeping with the 'Inns' found in New York City. It is all the better for this.Our stay over new year was excellent - from the friendly, efficient check-in; stylish, modern, clean bedrooms; bathrooms you actually want to use (though many rooms simply have walk-in showers rather than a bath so worth checking if that is important to you); 'The Living' where drinks and snacks are available 24/7 - all complimentary - and internet access is free; to the more than sufficient breakfasts served in the kitchen. If you are looking for pomp and ceremony (you know the sort of thing - your poached eggs brought to you covered in a silver dome at breakfast), then Banks isn't for you. If, however, you are content to request freshly cooked pancakes, french toast and feast of high quality fresh bread, jam, cheese and meat at breakfast and prefer a more relaxed hotel stay, this place is perfect.Re comments below regarding the policy of not taking drinks to your room. This is nonsense. Yes, the drinks are for sharing so it is bad form to take a bottle of champagne up to your room, but we (and other guests) were never stopped from taking glasses of wine  champagne, bottles of beer, cups of coffee etc. to our room. As we stayed over new year, a half bottle of champagne was left on our bed - a nice guesture. There is also a well stocked mini bar in each room along with decanters of gin, congac and whisky.For a City Centre base in Amsterdam, Banks Mansion is faultless. I wish every city had an equivalent hotel to save us from the overpriced misery of bland, outdated, business hotels that charge 鈧?0+ for a substandard breakfast.If I had to critique it would be twofold: 1) our loo roll supplies weren't topped up (thoug remedied by a phonecall) and 2) local taxes payable on checkout were unexpected. That said, as everything else was included in the room rate, the bill on checkout was considerably smaller than is usually the case!

<Author>suzweise
<Content>Great Hotel There is a reason that Banks Mansion is rated number 2 among hotels in Amsterdam on the tripadvisor website--it's simply a great hotel. As other reviewers have stated, the hotel staff is friendly and helpful with directions and restaurant recommendations, the rooms and beds are comfortable, and the complimentary breakfast, snacks and drinks only add to make your stay more enjoyable.My husband and I stayed at Banks Mansion in early December 2006 with two friends. Our friends are rather picky about where they stay, so I spent a lot of time researching various hotels in Amsterdam based on the location, cost and amenities. We booked the Christmas Shopping arrangement package on the Banks Mansion webiste at a good rate considering everything that was included with it. We were fortunate to be visiting during Sinterklaasavod (December 5th), when Sinter Klaas, along with his helper, Zwarte Piet, arrive to launch the Christmas season. As a part of this celebration, the hotel left cookies at our door as a gift. I have visited Amsterdam in the summer, spring and winter, and I've found December to be one of the best times there because of Sinterklassavod and the Christmas markets. Moreover, of all of the hotels I've stayed in during those visits, none compares with the comfort of Banks Mansion.

<Author>Mimiasovitch
<Content>Fabulous Having stayed in various other hotels over the years we booked the Banks Mansion on the strength of Trip Advisor reviews. We really weren't disappointed. We arrived early expecting to have to leave our luggage until later, but were shown to our room straight away. The room was a good size, very clean and attractive, and most importantly the bed was VERY comfortable.The staff were all lovely, breakfast was great, the free bar is a lovely idea and the shower was fantastic. Next time I will make sure I book a bath, but that is my only gripe. We had booked a canal view room, but whilst that sounds nice we were out and about, walking around the canals. Maybe its a good idea to ensure that the room is quieter. The location was excellent, within walking distance of everywhere we wanted to go. The walking also helped stave off the inevitable weight gain that follows too many pancakes.We love this city and visit every year. Next year we'll definately stay here again.

<Author>Manchester-England
<Content>loved it!! I've only stayed in one other hotel in Amsterdam, a soulless Marriott type...but whilst walking round the city i couldn't see any hotel as nice as the Banks Mansion.Its got something....not especially from the outside...and not especially the area, which whilst central didnt have the best view from the side windows (take aways and graffiti) but the inside is just wonderful!Cosy, warm, beautifully decorated, light, modern but with a twenties style about it. Just lovely!The staff are fantastic. Friendly, helpful and without being forced!We got chatting to some guys who were staying in the hotel who told us that the night before they had asked for a cab to be ordered as it was pouring down outside. The taxi still hadnt turned up ten minutes later so the receptionist actually stood outside and flagged one down for them!! Does that not say it all?The free drinks/food thing is great. Not really free of course as Banks Mansion is pretty expensive...but the concept works...it feels good to have drinks and snacks on tap without the irksome task of totting up your bar bill at the end of the night.....Rooms lovely, breakfast great and again helpful staff here too.The outside areas by the way, i may have been a bit harsh. It is in the nicer parts of Amsterdam, along a canal, and not far from the flower marketAnyway, we wouldnt stay anywhere else in Amsterdam, it was pretty near perfect.

<Author>errant
<Content>Banks Mansion -- sometimes two stars, sometimes four After a long flight across the Atlantic and a six hour layover in London, we were pathetically grateful to finally reach the Banks Mansion. Our canal view room, booked weeks before our trip, wasn't available. Instead, we were shown to a dark room facing, well, nothing.Not an auspicious start! Two stars or less.Room 312, however, had its good side. The bed was very comfortable and the Banks Mansion offers a menu of five different types of pillows, for any kind of firmness or softness you desire. The four pillows already in the room suited us just fine, and I'm a pillow snob. Four stars.The bathroom was also another definite plus. It was very big. The separate shower was large with a huge shower head and loads of water pressure. The tub was great for a deep soak and you faced away from the toilet. I love my bubble baths but I hate staring at a toilet for the duration of my bath. Four stars. However, the towels were tiny and the soap/shampoo situation was pretty miserly. Also, a face towel that went astray sat at the back of the cabinet floor for four days. The cleaner never spotted it though the rest of the bathroom was sparkling. Two stars.Everybody raves about the free booze and snacks. Yes, there are decanters of cognac, gin and whiskey on the bedside table. If that's your thing then I guess it's pretty exciting. I'm a bit of a cynic and always wonder what other guests may have added to the mixture. But, hey, that's just me. There is a mini bar with water, juice, pop and two Heinekens. I must admit that was a nice touch. Also, the bar downstairs had lashings of red and white wine, beers, pops, sparkling and flat waters, coffee, tea, liqueurs, you name it. Help yourself. Four stars.Breakfast (included) was great. No quibbles there. It was open from 7-10:30 during the week and until 11 on the weekend. Very civilized. The usual ham, cheese, muesli, yogurt mix but also the added bonus of omelets, pancakes and porridge made fresh to order. Four stars.The staff were WONDERFUL. Especially Michel. He deftly saved every two star situation and made it into a four. He knew we were disappointed about our room change and made sure a chilled bottle of champagne was waiting for us the next evening as well as an offer to change rooms as soon as a canal view was available (we elected to stay where we were because it was too much of a hassle to re-pack). Noticing our interest in dining, he gave us a fabulous book on Amsterdam restaurants and insisted we keep it. He also gave us great recommendations. A charming man and a real asset to the hotel. As were the rest of the staff. Five stars!Would we go back? We debated this and decided, yeah, we would. By the way, enjoy Amsterdam. It is a FABULOUS city!  
<Date>Nov 1, 2006

<Author>leavinrichmond
<Content>The Best My best friend and I stayed here for 3 nights and we definitely could have stayed longer. The Staff :Very friendly and attentive. Henry, who was on duty when we arrived, saw us exiting our taxi and struggling with our luggage came outside to assist us. After insisting on taking our luggage to the room, he stayed and explained everything the hotel had to offer in detail. At dinner time we asked the clerk at the front desk about a good restaurant in the area and he directed us to a very good Italian restaurant on the corner, Point Arcata. They were also very helpful in assisting us when we had to ship some of our purchases home going so far as to packing them for us.Rooms:Typical small European room but decorated very nicely. The bathroom was very large with a huge tub for relaxing in. Plush terrycloth robes and slippers are provided for you so all you need are your pajamas.Amenities:An extensive breakfast was included in our room price and it was worth every cent. No simple rolls and coffee here! The food and service was excellent! If you stay here, make sure you take advantage of the coffee and drinks that are free and the good snacks that are put out 3 times a day. Internet access is free and lobby is a beautiful place to sit and enjoy the scenery outside (the hotel is near a canal), or to read a book.

<Author>dbw18
<Content>Disappointing I booked this hotel on the strength of the reviews I read on Trip Adviser, as I wanted something really special for my wife鈥檚 50th birthday.I emailed the hotel before our stay to ask them to provide some flowers for my wife, to be in the room when we arrived. (I have now seen on a previous review that someone else did this successfully). I was told that this would be no problem. I also asked them to recommend a restaurant and book a table for the Friday night of our stay.When we arrived there were no flowers in the room so I went down to reception to find out why. The receptionist, who had replied to my email, said that he had forgotten to order the flowers. However he said he would get onto it straight away. Having forgotten the flowers I checked with him that he had booked the table at the restaurant. He assured me that this had been done. The flowers soon turned up and I was not charged for them.The room was great but during the first night my wife and I were kept awake by a rather noisy fan, which was directly over our bed. The next day we reported this and asked if it could be switched off. We were told that it could not be switched off but that it would be seen to. Later that day we were told that the filter had been changed. This did not make it any quieter and we had to live with the noise for the duration of our stay. There was also a stain on the floor of the room. Beware of room 411鈥檚 noisy fan!On the Friday evening we turned up at Het Tuynhuys restaurant on Reguliersdwarsstraat and we were told that they had no record of our booking and that they were full for the evening. They rang our hotel and the receptionist said that he could not remember if he had actually booked the meal. The staff at the restaurant felt sorry for us and worked hard to find us a table and in half an hour we were sat down ready to order. The food is fabulous and the service first rate. We highly recommend it and a special thank you to the manager and Nichole.We would agree with other reviews that this hotel is in an excellent location close to many of the attractions and that the free drinks and snacks are a bonus.We would also agree that the front office desk is friendly but not skilled at handling requests. They did not seem to know very much when asked general enquires about Amsterdam. When we tried to check out some information about buying tickets for some of the attractions they could not help us. We were often kept waiting and then when we were being dealt with; the staff broke away and talked to someone else. On one occasion the receptionist had to ask a senior member of staff three times about a simple enquiry. Not once did the senior member of staff come out and deal with the issue. More training is clearly needed in customer care and the art of concentration.Amsterdam has so much to offer and we would recommend hiring a bike (Mac Bike) to explore and the Sauna Deco at Herengracht 115 Grachtengordel. With all the cycling and walking you will do it is worth spending some time relaxing and Sauna Deco is a great place to do it. They provide good refreshments.Banks Mansion clearly has many good features and facilities, however for us it was let down by the carelessness of the staff.Where was Nina? (Mentioned in previous reviews). Come back all is forgiven!

<Author>Missyjas
<Content>Great hotel! My husband and I stayed at the Banks Mansion from Sept. 21-26 on vacation. It truly is a great place. The staff is friendly and helpful. The free internet is a great perk as well as all inclusive drinks in the main lobby and in your room. Breakfast was great as well. The rooms were clean, but very small. There is a nice bureau for hanging clothes and some shelves, but we had no place to store our luggage. The canal view was nice to have, but I wouldn't have been comfortable there for an entire weeks stay due to the small quarters. My only other complaint is that the stand-up shower we had leaked horribly. It would flood the ENTIRE bathroom floor, and when I say entire I mean it! We notified the front desk, but all that was provided to us was extra towels. So, I must admit having 3-4 soaking wet towels on the small bathroom floor after your shower was pretty much a pain. The location is great; within walking distance to most everything and to some great restaurants recommended by the front desk staff. We never used the public transit because we were able to walk everywhere. I would definitely stay here again!

<Content>Banks Mansion-Great! We stayed at the Banks Mansion after a 9 day Baltic cruise. We were spoiled from the service on the ship and Banks Mansion did not disappoint.Check in was easy. <Author>Joteddy
<Content>Fantastic Banks Mansion! Stayed at Banks Mansion for 3 nights on 25th August 06, for mine  husband's 10th wedding anniversary (without our kids hurray!! - thanks mum and dad for looking after them!). Was very excited about staying at the hotel, especially after reading so many positive reviews on trip advisor. Arrived after a short delay on our flight at around 7 pm, we were greeted by 'Nina' on Reception, who was very friendly. We were given room 201 which had a view overlooking the Herengracht canal, and our window was directly opposite the Mayor of Amsterdam's house!! Lovely room, large bed with a chair/footstool at the side. Nice shower-room in art-deco style with a lovely big shower cubicle. The shower leaked onto the floor each time so we had to make good use of the bath mat, but it wasnt worth complaining about! Loved the plasma tv on the wall, and the dvd player. Also enjoyed the free decanters of drink - gin, brandy and whiskey. We made it to breakfast 2 of our 3 mornings, very nice but found the girl who made the omelettes/french toast etc a bit stroppy. I think she was just a bit stressed as she had been left alone by her colleagues, but even so she was a bit rude! (I only asked if there was another loaf of bread as when we arrived in the breakfast room there was none!). (on Sundays the breakfast room is open until 11, we had arrived at approx. 10:20 - so obviously we expected to have bread available)! However, dont let this put you off, the hotel is great in general!We made good use of the 'living area' where they provide free coffee and pastries in the mornings, alcoholic drinks (more or less everything you can think of) and nuts/doritos/dips etc in the afternoon/evening. Oh, and free use of the internet if you need it. The hotel was in an excellent location, everything we were interested in seeing was within a 10 minute walk. We had a lovely meal (probably the nicest meal we've ever had - and we've eaten in a fair few restaurants!), at Casa di David which is located on the Singel, a 7 minute walk from Banks Mansion. To start we shared bruschetta with mozzarella and pesto - delicious. My husband then had a plain old spaghetti bolognaise - but said it was the best he'd ever eaten! I had kebabs of king prawn  poached salmon, on a bed of green beans with parmesan dressing - gorrrrgeous! This was served with saute potatoes. The food was lovely, the setting lovely, waiters very friendly, lovely atmosphere. (by the way we got Nina at Banks Mansion to reserve us a table as we'd tried to get in on the Friday night but couldnt).We also ate lunch at Cafe de Kroon in Rembrandtplein, just a snack, but it was a lovely sunny day and nice to people-watch for an hour or so!We also tried a 'coffee shop'. We stayed away from the tourist-y ones, and went to a more 'locals' type coffee shop. Had a great atmosphere, with funky dance music playing. Had a wander through the Red Light District - what an eye-opener!!! Also did a canal boat tour, during the day, this was really enjoyable too.We spent one morning shopping in Kalverstraat - a few nice clothes shops (some designer, some high street), everything a bit cheaper than the UK. All in all, will definitely go back to Amsterdam one day, and will stay at Banks Mansion!  
<Date>Aug 30, 2006

<Content>Absolutely loved this hotel! In no uncertain terms, Banks Mansion was an absolutely stellar experience! We were a family of 3 (mom, 18 yr. old  20 yr. old) in two rooms (one deluxe dbl w/ partial canal view) and (one deluxe single with canal view) for 6 nights. Rooms were spacious enough (given European standards), bathrooms w/ rain showers  hand showers(no bathtubs), hairdryers  toiletries provided, great air-conditioning and unlimited free mini bar (including alcoholic drinks). The breakfasts are generous, smoked salmon, cheese, meats, cereals, breads  pastries, fruit, yogurt, scrambled eggs, bacon, sausage with the addition of being able to order eggs  omelets, pancakes and french toast. The Living Area has free bar for alcoholic  non-alcoholic drinks and 2 computers for free internet access 24/7. Papers and magazines are provided and it's very comfortable to just be able to sit and relax before or after heading out for sightseeing. In addtion, they provide snacks (ranging from bread, olive spreads  nuts to sushi to pastries) every afternoon.It is perfectly located, easy to walk to just about everywhere! But most importantly was how friendly, warm and helpful the staff was at Banks Mansion! Every restaurant they recommended was great, directions provided to everything. I cannot recommend this hotel highly enough, whether traveling as a family (kids 10  up) or as a couple, it was a most welcome respite to many European hotels.

<Author>jzking
<Content>Amazing Location, Nice Hotel This hotel is very nice, especially in regards to its location. Being located on the southern part of Herengracht, it is close to everything. So, this is defenitely a strong point for this hotel. As far as cleanliness and styling, this hotel gets good marks. The rooms have a modern business feel that isn't formulated like many large hotels. The lobby has a nice bar with complimentary cokes, water, juices, snacks, etc. Breakfast was especially enjoyable with a full menu and a chef to make omellets, pancakes, and the like. The customer service is very good for a 3* hotel although, one of the night clerks was somewhat overbearing when it came to getting a water from the mini bar. Definetly has more of a 5* feel than 3*. We got a nightly rate of 199 euros which I thought was very reasonable considering the location and amenities. A lot of people have knocked this hotel on the price but I don't think their complaints have much merit. All things considered such as location, service, and amenities, I highly recommend this hotel to small families, couples, and business traverlers alike.

<Author>Stanat
<Content>perfect This is my first review on-line and if you keep on reading you'll find out why. After booking the hotel through a travel website, we contacted the hotel directly and asked if we could be upgraded because we were celebrating our anniversary. When we arrived we were greeted as if we were old friends. We were told that we had the option of picking from 3 different rooms. When we entered the first room, on the bed was a porcelain figurine of a dutch boy and girl puckering up to kiss and a note stating  Welcome to the Banks Mansion. We are so pleased that you chose us to celebrate your anniversary. The room was beautiful, facing the front of the hotel on the corner with views of the canal in either direction. The room was large even by american standards. The room had double beds pushed together, a large armchair wth footstool, a desk with a mirror, a tall closet and plenty of space to walk around. The bathroom had a shower stall with a refreshing rain showerhead, a bathtub which could also be used for showering and the sink was higher than ordinary making for easier use. The room had AC which we could control which we found to be unusual in european hotels and which we were very grateful for because we hit a hot spell in Europe. Needless to say, we never viewed the other two rooms.  The  living and the mini in roombar along with the three decanters of gin, whiskey and cognac were as advertised and included in the room price, plentiful and useable 24 hours. I shouldn't forget to mention free internet use. The breakfast was varied and plentiful. There was an egg, etc. station where you could order what you wanted. The cook remembered and asked us if we wanted the same order as we ordered the day before. The only drawback is that the kitchen has no AC which on some days, because of the hot spell, made it uncomfortable.  If that were not enough, the staff was extra-ordinary. They were always pleasant, smiling and very helpful. Nothing that is asked is too much for them. Don't miss this place. It is an unique experience.
